From manish.tomar at gmail.com  Tue May  1 10:51:24 2007
From: manish.tomar at gmail.com (Manish Tomar)
Date: Tue May  1 10:51:34 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] FC6 problem
Message-ID: <afd09a2a0704302221j47f4c178je249076f9045fd3e@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

I installed FC6 in my x86 machine with Intel motherboard. It's installed
properly but I am facing two major problems:

1. The keys double quotes (") and at symbol (@) got interchanged, i.e.
pressing one displays other one on screen. I posted this prob to
linuxquestions.com (
http://www.linuxquestions.org/questions/showthread.php?t=505554) and added
following in xorg.conf file (I think):
Section "InputDevice"
Identifier "Keyboard0"
Driver "kbd"
Option "XkbModel" "pc105"
Option "XkbLayout" "us"
Option "XkbVariant" "intl"
EndSection
This fixed the @ key but double quotes still doesn't come properly.
2. I am able to ping websites like google.com & yahoo.com but not able to
connect to them using the browser or telnet. Is there a problem with TCP
stack?

-- 
Regards,
Manish
(http://manishtomar.blogspot.com/)

From shakthimaan at gmail.com  Tue May  1 19:18:02 2007
From: shakthimaan at gmail.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Tue May  1 19:18:11 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Mailing list guidelines: monthly reminder
Message-ID: <d16b1c80705010648q3deaba71nfde04cb8fe940377@mail.gmail.com>

Mailing List Guidelines

1. Use a proper subject line.

2. Do not troll in the mailing list

Link: http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet_troll

3. Use [OT] for off-topic, non-technical discussions. But, don't
misuse this to start flame wars or to troll in the mailing list.

4. Do not top-post:

Link: http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Top-posting

Example of a top-post:

Because it messes up the order in which
people normally read text.
> > Why is top-posting
> > such a bad thing?
Top-posting.
> > What is the most
> > annoying thing in e-mail?

Always use bottom-posting.

> What is your name ?
My name is ILUGC.

5. Do not over-quote:

Example of an over-quote:

>>> On Friday you said
>>> blah blah blah
>> On Saturday you said
>> foo foo foo
> On Sunday you said
> foobar

6. Do not post HTML messages

7. Do not recycle messages

8. Do not send attachments

9. Do not attach obnoxious, nonsensical legal disclaimers. If your
company uses disclaimers, don't use your company ID for the mailing
list.

10. Do not reply to a digest. (If you are in digest mode and want to
reply to a post use ILUGC Gmane blog interface.

Link: http://blog.gmane.org/gmane.org.user-groups.linux.ilugc

11. Search for answers for your questions/problems in google.com or
any other search engine before posting your query to the mailing list.

If any of the above are not clear to you, Please read the detailed
list guidelines:

Link: http://www.catb.org/~esr/faqs/smart-questions.html

12. Do not post messages in all capital letters. Mails in CAPS is
considered rude and is similar to shouting during a conversation.

13. If you or your company is into GNU/Linux migration, or you want
help into GNU/Linux migration, check here:
http://www.chennailug.org/wiki/GNU_Linux_migration

14. If you are looking for GNU/Linux distro CDs please check here:
http://www.chennailug.org/wiki/CDs_for_Grab

15. Following these guidelines could be helpful
http://people.debian.org/~enrico/dcg/

16. Don't send season's greetings or birthday invites to the group.
Its not mailing list etiquette.

We must use the above guidelines to maintain better readability,
proper archives, efficient bandwidth usage, etc.

I would stick to using a bluetooth enabled Phone with the computer. 
Bluetooth Phones are a lot cheaper than the Data Card and youve got the 
Advantage of using your phone with other Devices Like PDAs, Desktop 
Computers and so on whereas with the PCMCIA Data Card you are restricted 
to Notebook computers. Also, I am quite sure all major OSs support 
bluetooth NAP or Dial up Service these days so i don't think it will be 
a problem to get things working.

Google Gives the Answer: searced for "Minimal Linux Distro with IPV6 
Support"

Came up with http://www.nycwireless.net/pebble

This appears to be one of these Specialist OSs based on Debian Linux 
targeted at Network Devices based on The Soekris Boards. But the ReadMe 
Says:

"Will it run on a standard old pentium PC:
	It should run fine on a standard PC.  For development I run it
on my laptops.  Minimum requirement is a 486 processor.  32mb of ram is
recommended, though you can probably get away with less, especially if
you don't start NoCatAuth."

So i guess it will install with no problems on your Pc, and the 
changelog says that IPV6 support is bundled since v.19 (which happens to 
have been the second public release) and all you need to get it working 
is apt-get install ipv6

Joe Steeve wrote:
> 
> After going through some similar problems with the bdb backend on older
> Subversion releases, i moved to the fsfs backend. It has not given me a
> problem since. New versions of svn support the 'fsfs' backend as a default.
> 

+1 for fsfs. It uses flat files instead of a db to store changes, so
much less chances of db locks, and all the related niggles. You can
convert your bdb repos to fsfs:

http://svn.haxx.se/users/archive-2005-02/0557.shtml

HTH,
V.

From abhas at deeproot.co.in  Wed May  2 15:50:27 2007
From: abhas at deeproot.co.in (Abhas Abhinav)
Date: Wed May  2 16:17:00 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] problem with subversion/berkelydb
In-Reply-To: <D805C874-B79E-472D-B222-1F8612789EE4@thenilgiris.com>
References: <D805C874-B79E-472D-B222-1F8612789EE4@thenilgiris.com>
Message-ID: <200705021550.27799.abhas@deeproot.co.in>

On Wednesday 02 May 2007 7:58:49 am Kenneth Gonsalves wrote:
> i have a server with several subversion repositories. I keep getting
> berkelydb errors and have to run svnadmin recover, sometimes more
> than once a week. Although all the repostiories are under the same
> directory, they get clobbered at different times. There doesnt seem
> to be any correlation between size of repo or amount of use and
> number of times it gets corrupt. Any clues - this is driving me nuts.

We had faced the same problem many times before! About a year back we migrated 
out of using BerkleyDB as the filesystem for the SVN repository to using FSFS 
as the filesystem. FSFS uses plain files (on your filesystem) to store the 
repository and does not require or use BerkleyDB at all. Our repository size 
and number of users have only grown after our shift we've not seen any 
performance drop. We have, however, got rid of those nasty BerleyDB errors.

To convert your existing repository to the FSFS format, you will need to first 
take a dump of your repository (svnadmin dump), then create a new repository 
with FSFS format (svnadmin create /repos/path --fs-type fsfs) and then import 
the earlier SVN dump (svnadmin load).

You should not face these problems with your SVN again.

Hope this helps...

Cheers, Abhas.
-- 
i-take-charge at DeepRoot Linux
http://www.deeproot.in / +91 (80) 4112 4784 / 85
Getting GNU/Linux to work for you. Faster. Better. Today. Every way.

> On 02-May-07, at 4:46 PM, Kamesh Jayachandran wrote:
> >Subversion is unstoppable.
> 
> are you sure? with distributed version control systems gaining share  
> isnt subversion becoming outdated?

I'm glad you said it first! I've been biting my tongue on the recent svn
thread, wanting to say "just use {darcs|arch|bzr}". The only use-case I
see for SVN is in shops where CVS-style development is so entrenched
that moving to a less-warty system is the biggest change inertia will
allow. Yes, there's a bit of a learning curve (especially un-learning
CVS -- remember how annoying that was when you first had to use it) but
I find Darcs, and the detailed history of my code that it provides, to
be an excellent productivity enhancer once adopted on a project.

Regards,

Doran

You can still use Subversion for decentralized development using the
svk plugin. It is written in perl, stable and cool plugin one would
love to use. But yeah, it is a nice to have feature in Subversion
during long run. But given the amount of popularity Subversion gains
in recent times, I'm unsure how many users are considering this
feature as a bottle-neck to use Subversion. For what is worth, the
count of Subversion users are doubling every 5 months.

OTOH, I'll not recommend bzr to corporates, not because of it's
nature, but because of it's current state. If i am right, it is still
in beta and they are actively working towards to release the first
stable version 1.0 as early as possible.

Check out this version control comparison chart to know the pros/cons
of every version control system.

From srsy70 at gmail.com  Wed May  2 19:51:53 2007
From: srsy70 at gmail.com (S.Ramaswamy)
Date: Wed May  2 19:52:04 2007
Subject: Centralized vs Distributed Version Control (was: Re: [Ilugc]
	Subversion Open House @ CollabNet Chennai)
Message-ID: <d60e5b0f0705020721r6f2004d2l4b9caf15dccfe64f@mail.gmail.com>

>
> are you sure? with distributed version control systems gaining share
> isnt subversion becoming outdated?
>

Subversion is outdated in the same way "Windows is outdated". Our
community has never lagged behind when it comes to wishful thinking
;-)

Honestly, I think a lot of the uptake with DVCSs is because a lot of
cool kids are doing it. :-D (damn, 2nd smiley) Most development
efforts, both corporate and open source development tend to have a
centralized way of doing things. I see real manageability issues with
DVCSs if it's unleashed into an inexperienced team with varying
experience/skill levels. The Mozilla developers recently decided to go
with Mercurial, which is distributed - I suspect what works for
developers who write Firefox may not work with "Average Joe/Janardhan"
types. Git works well for the kernel, because kernel dev. has it's own
peculiar development model - Check out Greg Hudson's article.  Besides
All open source projects will continue to have ***one*** official
release only in the near future. Even if you have the ability to
cherry pick features from unofficial branches, how many people are
going to use it ? Maybe DVCSs will only increase the fragmentation in
open source projects.

Ramaswamy

From doran+clug at down-with-gravity.org  Wed May  2 20:59:48 2007
From: doran+clug at down-with-gravity.org (Doran)
Date: Wed May  2 20:59:56 2007
Subject: Centralized vs Distributed Version Control (was: Re: [Ilugc]
	Subversion Open House @ CollabNet Chennai)
In-Reply-To: <d60e5b0f0705020721r6f2004d2l4b9caf15dccfe64f@mail.gmail.com>
References: <d60e5b0f0705020721r6f2004d2l4b9caf15dccfe64f@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20070502152948.GU15885@burns.dreamhost.com>

On Wed, May 02, 2007 at 07:51:53PM +0530, S.Ramaswamy wrote:
> Subversion is outdated in the same way "Windows is outdated". Our
> community has never lagged behind when it comes to wishful thinking
> ;-)

Amen to that.

Damn, I was trying not to dive back into this thread, but I have to
disagree with you on management issues: *many* projects using Darcs have
a single, central, canonical repository, and distributed branches are
merely for individual developers to hack on. This provides great
freeedom: while hacking on a project like this, I can make changes
willy-nilly in my development branch and not worry about cluttering up
the changelog of the central repository. I can even have my editor
commit the change every time I save to compile or test or lint the code,
without having to worry about the effects of maybe hundreds of commits a
day on the central repository. As I'm going, I get all the advantages of
version control -- mostly being able to inspect the changes on a number
of scales. When I have the code in a stable state, I can package up my
patches and send them as a single change -- perhaps by e-mail, where
appropriate hooks will run a test suite against it before committing it
to the main branch. This sort of model is approached by SVN's
lightweight branching, but it doesn't go far enough and isn't exploited
well enough in the majority of cases.

Also, I've worked in a number of places (on and off dev teams, but
mostly off them, attempting to support the developers) where the VCS is
seen merely as a backup tool. Changes get checked in and history is
ignored. Branches are under-utilised. Bug-ridden code or even cruft such
as temp files get checked in, and nobody cleans it up until stuff really
starts breaking. Developers in such an environment rapidly lose any
sense of ownership of the code, or craftsmanly pride in what they have
produced.

For sure, this is a social issue more than a technical one, and a number
of underlying social issues in programming for cash are exposed, but I
see it partly as a legacy of poor tools. Back in the day, using RCS/CVS,
there were two ways to go: either check in every little change and deal
with the history becoming overloaded with "fixed typo" and similarly
pointless cruft, or carefully hone whatever you do to make it a work of
art before checking it in. Naturally, neither extreme has ever been
achieved for more than a dozen checkins so we end up with the worst of
both worlds: a history that provides little more than meaningless
statistics for managers to get excited about ("Woo so-and-so checked in
eleventy-thousand lines of code this year!" never mind half of those
were fixing his own mistakes), and lack of access to good differencing
tools when it matters most: making incremental changes.

SVN goes a long way to correcting this, if its branches are properly
utilised (by which I mean: heavily, with a lightweight structure in
place).  But unfortunately, it suffers from legacy in some of the same
ways CVS does:while a "long term goal" is to achieve DVCS this isn't
something that can be bolted on, much as repository-wide versioning
can't just be bolted on to RCS; and even moreso those coming to it too
often see it as another member of the CVS line to be treated in the same
way. The proper use of DVC is actually a radically different way of
thinking, where the code is not static but is interacted with at every
stage as a changing entity with all those changes visible. This makes
regression-type bugs difficult to introduce, makes many types of
refactorings unbelievably easier, encourages modular code and generally
seems to lead to much more polished code.


So in summary, I'm a verbose fanboy. And I'm probably too hard on SVN.
It's no coincidence that the Darcs and Haskell worlds have so much
overlap, which harks back to the point that I quoted. But don't let that
put you off, the un-learning curve for doing version control the wrong
way (CVS) is much less than that for programming the wrong way (Java).
But now I've probably turned off or at least confused the Java fans, so
I'll stop with my foot approaching my mouth.


Doran

> seen merely as a backup tool. Changes get checked in and history is
> ignored. Branches are under-utilised. Bug-ridden code or even cruft such
> as temp files get checked in, and nobody cleans it up until stuff really
> starts breaking. Developers in such an environment rapidly lose any
> sense of ownership of the code, or craftsmanly pride in what they have
> produced.

That's a classical example for a real *bad* project execution. Why do
want to own pride for your work when you work in a project? When you
work in a project, you should not be bothered about your individual
craftsmanship, but you should work for goodness of the project.

> For sure, this is a social issue more than a technical one, and a number
> of underlying social issues in programming for cash are exposed, but I
> see it partly as a legacy of poor tools. Back in the day, using RCS/CVS,
> there were two ways to go: either check in every little change and deal
> with the history becoming overloaded with "fixed typo" and similarly
> pointless cruft, or carefully hone whatever you do to make it a work of
> art before checking it in. Naturally, neither extreme has ever been
> achieved for more than a dozen checkins so we end up with the worst of
> both worlds: a history that provides little more than meaningless
> statistics for managers to get excited about ("Woo so-and-so checked in
> eleventy-thousand lines of code this year!" never mind half of those
> were fixing his own mistakes), and lack of access to good differencing
> tools when it matters most: making incremental changes.

And again, it is one such example for poor practice. I suggest you to
observe the discussion among the developers (may be in a dev@ mailing
list) of any of open source project to know the typical practice.
-- 
Regards,
Bhuvaneswaran
www.symonds.net/~bhuvan/
GPG: 0x7A13E5B0

On Wed, 2007-05-02 at 18:43 +0530, ramprasad wrote:
> Hi,
> I am trying to install a wireless sniffer(tcpdump) on Linux(RH 9).
> I have a Dlink PCI Card which comes with a ralink chipset.
> 
> I am able to put the card in Monitor mode but it doesn't show the contents
> of the packets when tcpdump is used.
> When the card is put in Infrastructure mode using iwconfig, I am able to see
> the packets that are sent to the BSSID that I had configured for the card
> using iwconfig.
> 
> Is it possible to see all the packets using tcpdump ? Any ideas why I am not
> able to see the contents of the packets(beacons etc)
> 

I tried using tcpdump with an Atheros chipset in Monitor mode and was
able to see all the packets.
Saving the dump from tcpdump and opening the file in Wireshark also
worked fine. Wireshark deciphered all the packets perfectly.

My version of tcpdump is :

	tcpdump version 3.9.5
	libpcap version 0.9.5

The commands I used:

	sudo tcpdump -i ath1 -s 0 -n -vvv -XX
	sudo tcpdump -i ath1 -s 0 -n -vvv -XX -w raw.dump

I don't have a card with a ralink chipset, so can't help you there :)

regards,
Sujith.

From tshrinivasan at gmail.com  Thu May  3 10:46:48 2007
From: tshrinivasan at gmail.com (Shrinivasan)
Date: Thu May  3 10:46:26 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] prevent files from deleting even by root itself
In-Reply-To: <200705031031.30732.tshrinivasan@gmail.com>
References: <200705031031.30732.tshrinivasan@gmail.com>
Message-ID: <200705031046.48451.tshrinivasan@gmail.com>

On Thursday 03 May 2007 10:31, Shrinivasan wrote:
> Friends.
>
> I want to protect some files from deleting even from root itself.
>
> I have done it with chmod and some option.
> If you give that, the file can not be deleted even by root.


Myself found.

That is not chmod.
it is chattr

chattr +i <filename> to give protection.
chattr -i <filename> to revoke the protection.

-- 
dear,
T.Shrinivasan.

From rajsekhar.kvs at gmail.com  Thu May  3 14:42:54 2007
From: rajsekhar.kvs at gmail.com (rajasekhar kuppa)
Date: Thu May  3 14:43:04 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Using tcpdump with wireless interface(Ralink chipset)
In-Reply-To: <1178165336.5978.10.camel@sujith-lnx>
References: <def372aa0705020613p720919a6n1dc1ec4920d1ee0@mail.gmail.com>
	<1178165336.5978.10.camel@sujith-lnx>
Message-ID: <446cb7260705030212l7497b95dga8342a2b26b8d9f@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

 I am not saying that you cannot see the packets that are being transferred
on the network - you definitely can see it  -- but what you will be seeing
will only be the TCP/IP section of the frame but not the 802.11 frames ( for
example the management , beacons etc.) so do these commands give you the

lagging far behind if i am unaware of such developmentsin the wireless end.

instruction is in the email header or, how many of mailing lists we
know that do not have footers. So far, I don't see any mailing lists

exception?

size, I suggest to include the mailing list URL alone in the footer.

mailing list URL to unsubscribe from the mailing list is an unanswered
question!!

Subject: [Ilugc] Downloading using accelerators - suggestions needed

Hi,

I am have been trying to download Kubunty Fiesty Fawn DVD for the past
couple of weeks. Initially, only the Torrent version was available,
and I tried downloading using KTorrent. I wasn't happy with it, as I
couldn't schedule the downloads between 2 AM and 8 AM. I then switched
to Azures. It did a good job, but, I had the download directory
pointed towards a FAT32 file system. Kubuntu ISO is 4.3 GB :-).  I
cleaned up my EXT3 FS for download again. Torrent isn't all that fast
and many times, I couldn't find seeders.

By then the DVD ISO was available for download from FTP mirrors. AXEL
which did a great job of downloading the the CD version at 150 KBPS,
failed miserably by reporting the following
<SNIP>
File size: -2147483648 bytes
Opening output file kubuntu-7.04-dvd-i386.iso
Crappy filesystem/OS.. Working around. :-(
</SNIP>
I got the same error for both EXT3 and VFAT

I tried the good old wget with a cron job. it works but at 6 KBPS.

I downloaded prozilla source-code and compiled it. It now has a decent
speed of 60 KBPS. But, i am not able to provide more than one mirror
URL to prozilla. It does an automatic search with LYCOS for alternate
FTP URLs. But the internal search doe not return anything. There is no
way for me to supply my own list of URLs. Moreover, it cant accept
multiple HTTP URLs.

Is there any easier way to download faster using accelerators? one of
the main criteria is that, I have to start it using a CRON job and
kill it using another CRON job. (2AM to 8 AM limits).

In simple words: how do you download such huge files with a BSNL BB?

Cheers,
Natarajan

Since ubuntu is based on debian it should have jigdo. Since you have
CD version and some downloaded files, you can use jigdo. This will
construct cd/dvd image downloading only what is not available
locally.

You can schedule the job using cron. However it will not use any
accerlator. You will get single thread only.

use jigdo to download an Ubuntu DVD a few days back - unfortunately
the jigdo template file is in itself around 700 MB! And there are no
officially released jigdo files, the latest I could find was made on
18th april (nightly builds), while feisty was released on 19th. Some
on the forums complained of older packages (which were later updated)
as not being present on the ubuntu repositories, causing an error in
jigdo. So, like the OP, I settled back to a standard accelerated http
download using Prozilla.

From: Subir Pradhanang <subirbp@gmail.com>

Subject: [FOSS Nepal] Toshiba Italy mulls pre-loaded Linux notebooks
To: FOSS Nepal <foss-nepal@googlegroups.com>


Hi all,

Toshiba Italy mulls pre-loaded Linux notebooks

http://www.desktoplinux.com/news/NS9644921792.html

---
Toshiba's Italian channel sales and marketing operation reportedly is
considering offering pre-loaded Linux in its Tecra, Satellite,
Portege, and Qosmio notebook lines, according to a story published
online last week in the Il Sole newspaper.

Luigi Cattaneo, country manager for Toshiba's Italy Computer Systems
Division, reportedly acknowledged that Hewlett-Packard and Acer own
more than 50 percent of the Italian Windows laptop computer market,
and that one way for his company to move ahead would be to offer
pre-installed Linux as an option, the newspaper reported.

Cattaneo said that in order to make headway in the SMB (small- to
medium-sized business) market, his company would have to market
notebooks in the 500-Euro range, and to do that, a Linux OS would be a
requirement, the newspaper reported.

"The corporation is seriously talking about this, and we are
evaluating attentively the question," Cattaneo was quoted as having
said. "It is a potential business to which we do not want to close the
door."

A Toshiba spokesperson at the U.S. headquarters in Irvine, Calif., did
not have an immediate comment when reached by DesktopLinux.com.

The Il Sole article is available online in Italian, here.
---

Cheers,

From doran+clug at down-with-gravity.org  Fri May  4 22:17:04 2007
From: doran+clug at down-with-gravity.org (Doran)
Date: Fri May  4 22:17:11 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Compiler Design
In-Reply-To: <911086.1022.qm@web36811.mail.mud.yahoo.com>
References: <911086.1022.qm@web36811.mail.mud.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <20070504164704.GC20541@burns.dreamhost.com>

On Fri, May 04, 2007 at 09:22:59AM -0700, Amit Dey wrote:
> are gnu tools flex(lex) and bison(yacc) enough to create full fledged compilers like GCC?

In a word, no. flex+bison are parser generators -- this is an important
part of compilation, but not enough in itself. Also (I'm a little ruasty
on this point, so anyone, please correct me) they are for LR parsers and
in particular deal badly with ambiguity: C's grammar is a horrible thing
and building a parser for this is beyond the abilities of anything
reasonable.

But that's not to put a damper on your goals. Useful languages with less
pathological grammars (pascal comes to mind) can very well be parsed
with flex/bison. And the rest of compilation doesn't need to be that
difficult. At the next ILUGC meet I'll be introducing Scheme, which is a
wonderful little language for researching programming tool, and if you
have a better network connection than me I highly recommend googling
"the 90 minute scheme to C compiler", a talk given at a LUG somewhere in
Europe which delivers exactly what it promises in a nice little video.

I can probably dig up some other good online content on compilation if
you're interested.


Doran
From doran+clug at down-with-gravity.org  Fri May  4 22:37:37 2007
From: doran+clug at down-with-gravity.org (Doran)
Date: Fri May  4 22:37:43 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] M$ patent for sudo???
In-Reply-To: <69621d830705040904v588e2e5ds2e5c4be78de4b1c1@mail.gmail.com>
References: <69621d830705040904v588e2e5ds2e5c4be78de4b1c1@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20070504170737.GE20541@burns.dreamhost.com>

On Fri, May 04, 2007 at 10:04:19PM +0600, Zico wrote:
> What is this company`s problem??
> Always tries to get something which have been already created.
> They have enough money, but they cannot create anything by their own???
> 
> Check this:
> 
> http://ubuntulinuxtipstricks.blogspot.com/2007/05/did-microsoft-just-patent-sudo.html

A few points:

 * as much as I'm not a fan of Microsoft, I wouldn't level the charge of
   "no innovation" against them
 * show me a single software patent that wouldn't be invalidated by a
   reasonable court on the grounds of "prior invention" or even more so,
   being trivially obvious to anyone with an ounce of relevant expertise
 * this sounds more like "privilege seperation" a la sshd, than sudo:
   particularly in that it refers to a seperate, already running process
   rather than assuming a different UID. Not that this model is any
   newer than sudo .. I think VMS did something similar.

Actually, maybe I've missed something: why sudo? What does it do in
relation to this patent that su doesn't?


Doran

> stripped
> out by many e-mail clients when quoting.

when quoting, the proper way to do it is:
1. highlight the part you are going to quote
2. press 'reply'
3. if your mail client has any sense, you will get only the quoted  
material on the reply screen.

in this way, no extraneous matter enters the reply. It is silly to  
rely on '-- ' to strip out parts.

Now to poke a small hole in that mutt page up there, having used mutt
for the last 8 years or so.

Why Mutt is better than other text-based e-mail clients like Pine:
# Supports threads
#   Multiple instances can be run simultaneously
#   Colors

If you haven't seen 4.6x versions of pine (which have been around for
over two years now) they do all 3.

From srsy70 at gmail.com  Sat May  5 13:47:12 2007
From: srsy70 at gmail.com (S.Ramaswamy)
Date: Sat May  5 13:47:24 2007
Subject: Centralized vs Distributed Version Control (was: Re: [Ilugc]
	Subversion Open House @ CollabNet Chennai)
In-Reply-To: <20070502152948.GU15885@burns.dreamhost.com>
References: <d60e5b0f0705020721r6f2004d2l4b9caf15dccfe64f@mail.gmail.com>
	<20070502152948.GU15885@burns.dreamhost.com>
Message-ID: <d60e5b0f0705050117w21783bcdoe86eff44054b32c3@mail.gmail.com>

>
> Damn, I was trying not to dive back into this thread, but I have to
> disagree with you on management issues: *many* projects using Darcs have
> a single, central, canonical repository, and distributed branches are
> merely for individual developers to hack on.

Why can't you hack in the working copy of a centralized version control system ?

>This provides great
> freeedom: while hacking on a project like this, I can make changes
> willy-nilly in my development branch and not worry about cluttering up
> the changelog of the central repository. I can even have my editor
> commit the change every time I save to compile or test or lint the code,
> without having to worry about the effects of maybe hundreds of commits a
> day on the central repository. As I'm going, I get all the advantages of
> version control -- mostly being able to inspect the changes on a number
> of scales. When I have the code in a stable state, I can package up my
> patches and send them as a single change -- perhaps by e-mail, where
> appropriate hooks will run a test suite against it before committing it
> to the main branch. This sort of model is approached by SVN's
> lightweight branching, but it doesn't go far enough and isn't exploited
> well enough in the majority of cases.

The bunch of issues mentioned above indicate a failure to either
establish a sane branching policy or understand how branching works.

I am open to using DVCSs, but 'am yet to hear a cogent case made for them.

Ramaswamy

Look what is making headlines... M$ offering Windows on OLOP Laptops.

http://www.reuters.com/article/newsOne/idUSN0435704620070505
<QUOTE>
BOSTON (Reuters) - Microsoft Corp. hopes to develop a version of a $3
Windows software suite to run on low-cost laptops that a Massachusetts
foundation wants to send to the world's poorest children.

The software, designed for youngsters in developing nations, is being
tested on prototypes of small green-and-white laptops developed by the
One Laptop Per Child Foundation, Microsoft corporate vice president
Will Poole said on Friday.

The non-profit project plans to start mass production in September of
the so-called "XO" machines. They were designed specifically by the
foundation to run on the Linux operating system and other open-source
programs.

Linux is the main rival to Microsoft's Windows operating system. If
the machines run only Linux, Microsoft will lose out on an opportunity
to eventually expose tens of millions of children worldwide to its
Windows system.

One Laptop Per Child, founded by Massachusetts Institute of Technology
scientist Nicholas Negroponte, is selling them at $176 apiece to
governments, which will then distribute them to poor children.

Some governments have urged Microsoft, the world's largest software
maker, to equip those machines with Windows software instead of Linux
and other programs developed by the foundation, Poole told Reuters.

"They're coming to us and saying, 'Hey. If we buy these very nice,
low-cost laptops, can you give us a version of Windows and Office ...
Can you make that available for that nice bit of hardware'," Poole
said. "Our answer is 'maybe'."
Continued.....

</QUOTE>

From arnstein87 at gmail.com  Sat May  5 20:42:39 2007
From: arnstein87 at gmail.com (Arnold Noronha)
Date: Sat May  5 20:42:48 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Mount reiserfs with user write permissions
In-Reply-To: <20070505103103.GA2892@greatbear>
References: <20070505103103.GA2892@greatbear>
Message-ID: <3c52da3c0705050812u5c2e0c6bl6b0b6b357eebd465@mail.gmail.com>

On 5/5/07, Kumar Appaiah <akumar@ee.iitm.ac.in> wrote:
> Dear ILUGC,
>
> I have a reiserfs partition, which I'd like to mount with ordinary
> user writable permissions. However, an option of umask or uid in
> /etc/fstab alongside "defaults" warns me with an "invalid option"
> warning and fails to mount. What is the right way to mount it with
> user write permissions? Googling didn't get me far...
>

AFAIK, umask is supposed to be specific for FAT file systems, where
the files don't have a owner by default (you can see 'man mount' for
the filesystem specific options). Reiserfs has support for users and
groups, so mounting it should also honour this ownership.

In that sense, I would *guess* there isn't a "right" way to achieve
what you want.

HTH

--arnie
From akumar at ee.iitm.ac.in  Sat May  5 20:54:38 2007

On Sat, May 05, 2007 at 08:42:39PM +0530, Arnold Noronha wrote:
> AFAIK, umask is supposed to be specific for FAT file systems, where
> the files don't have a owner by default (you can see 'man mount' for
> the filesystem specific options). Reiserfs has support for users and
> groups, so mounting it should also honour this ownership.

I understand. So for filesystems which do have permissions, we can use
the same infrastructure.

From anant at kix.in  Sun May  6 03:37:12 2007
From: anant at kix.in (Anant Narayanan)
Date: Sun May  6 03:37:30 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Compiler Design
In-Reply-To: <20070504164704.GC20541@burns.dreamhost.com>
References: <911086.1022.qm@web36811.mail.mud.yahoo.com>
	<20070504164704.GC20541@burns.dreamhost.com>
Message-ID: <463D0010.2060805@kix.in>

> In a word, no. flex+bison are parser generators -- this is an important
> part of compilation, but not enough in itself. Also (I'm a little ruasty
> on this point, so anyone, please correct me) they are for LR parsers and
> in particular deal badly with ambiguity: C's grammar is a horrible thing
> and building a parser for this is beyond the abilities of anything
> reasonable.

There are lex token and bison grammar files available that recognize the
C language. Most programming languages can be recognized by a regular LR
parser.

Compilation is essentially a 6 stage process:

1) Analyze and split the source program to valid tokens
2) Parse the token stream and check for conformance to grammar
3) Convert the source token stream to an intermediate form (usually
Abstract Syntax Trees)
4) Parse the syntax tree and convert into a lower-level language
5) Perform optimizations, rinse and repeat
6) Finally convert the low-level language to assembly code for the
target architecture

Stages 1, 2 and 3 are usually part of the "front-end" of a compiler,
while stages 4, 5, 6 make up the "back-end".

Nothing like a good book to clear up the concepts. I recommend the
"Dragon book" on Compilers by Hopcroft and Ullman.

--
Anant

> OK, that seems to be all right. Thanks!
>
> But is it _the right way_? Of course, I am happy with this, but
> still...

it is... for fs's with a permission infrastructure, the best way to
give permissions is to use it. however, there's an alternative if you
just want to change the permissions for the current mount without
touching the filesystem (say u have to put it as ro, and have to give
read permissions otherwise not possible). try the fuse bindfs
filesystem, and enhanced userspace version of `mount --bind`

http://www.cs.helsinki.fi/u/partel/bindfs/

it moves on...

Subject: [Ilugc] Compiler Design
In-Reply-To: <911086.1022.qm@web36811.mail.mud.yahoo.com>
References: <911086.1022.qm@web36811.mail.mud.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <3f986c690705061946m452341e6uecff2d10d59ffe97@mail.gmail.com>

On 5/4/07, Amit Dey <eamitdey@yahoo.com> wrote:

> are gnu tools flex(lex) and bison(yacc) enough to create full fledged compilers like GCC?

Flex and Bison are excellent fully functional tools for compiler
building. I have myself used them to build compilers for toy languages
in compilers courses in grad school. Further they are the very tools
that are used in GCC itself. Certain front ends use flex, some don't.
But as far as I can remember all of them do use Bison as the parser
generator. In other words they are certainly "industrial strength"
tools.

That said, they are meant to solve two specific theoretically
well-understood sub-problems, which are particularly conducive to
"automatable" programming, in compiler construction...

-- 
Sriram Karra
Ph: 98463 38831, 044 - 2811 2630

Hari,

On 5/10/07, hari <rhariharan@gmail.com> wrote:
> Can someone suggest a good TV Tuner card that you have used on Linux
> (preferably on Windows too...) and that is available in India
> (chennai/bangalore).
> I am searching around for Hauppage, but cant find one.
> Intex/Techcom/Pinnacle/PixelView devices are flooding the market, but I dont
> know if are Linux Compatible and certainly dont want to find it out the hard
> way ;)

Hauppauge's are impossible to find in india. Only the cheap one's from
Pinnacle and Pixelview are available. They are well supported in
Linux. You need to use the bttv or the sa17XX modules for these cards.

More on the LinuxTV wiki:
http://www.linuxtv.org/v4lwiki/index.php/Cardlist.BTTV
http://www.linuxtv.org/v4lwiki/index.php/CARDLIST.saa7134

-Toufeeq

blog @ http://www.toufeeq.net

From anoopjohn at gmail.com  Thu May 10 21:17:51 2007
From: anoopjohn at gmail.com (Anoop John)
Date: Thu May 10 21:18:01 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] [OT]payment gateways
In-Reply-To: <feff2f50705100801v325e19akb72787736402c51f@mail.gmail.com>
References: <feff2f50705100801v325e19akb72787736402c51f@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <406f1f3f0705100847y66171378vc96b178e07419996@mail.gmail.com>

On 5/10/07, krishna chaitanya arava <krish.arava@gmail.com> wrote:
> We are coming out with a solution for collecting donations for an NGO in
> Lucknow, the donations would then be spent in building  children's home.
>
> 4214/-Rs for one time setup , 7% charges for credit card transactions and 4%
> for netbanking.
>
I must admit that paymet gateways are convenient. Buy why do you have
to pay an overhead of 2% or more per transaction for online payment?
Where are the bulk of payments coming form? India or outside India? It
makes sense to get payments from outside India through a payment
gateway but otherwise - it might be simply far more cheaper to go by
the traditional check or wire-transfer or dd method. Especially from
an NGO perspective you would want to optimize on every single paise
you get as donations.
For Indian donations you might want to open accounts in a few of the
top Indian banks and then give the account information for donors to
deposit the money directly. That should be the cheapest option. If
there are not too many donations it might be possible to just have
somebody enter the information into an online accounting system for
users to see
Cheers
Anoop John
www.zyxware.com

From sandip at deeproot.co.in  Fri May 11 14:38:19 2007
From: sandip at deeproot.co.in (sandip)
Date: Fri May 11 14:39:16 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Proudly Announcing http://gnulinux.in
Message-ID: <46443283.1000101@deeproot.co.in>

Greetings, friends!!

I'm Sandip Patel, a FOSS enthusiast based in Bangalore. A few of my
colleagues in DeepRoot Linux (www.deeproot.in - I am proud to be a
part of this _real_ Free Software Company), based both in Bangalore
and Ahmadabad, have been working with me, on a portal developed
and maintained for and by the GNU/Linux community in India. We are
keen that this site becomes a meeting point for FOSS enthusiasts
and contributors in different parts of the country.

On behalf of the maintainers of http://www.gnulinux.in I warmly
invite all ideas, contributions and suggestions that you have, to
enhance and enrich the website. We're thankful for all suggestions
we have already received, and have much to thank the FOSS
community.

Here's what is on offer:

 * FOSS knowledge-base: articles
 * Technical forum discussions
 * Personal blogs (of course on GNU/Linux and surrounding topics)
 * Posting space for GNU/Linux, FOSS related job offerings
 * Polls on various aspects of FOSS (and the website).

And in a short while we are also planing to setup:

 * Student support section
 * Mailing list
 * Wiki etc

So come, share your experiences, and join us in spreading the joy
of using GNU/Linux and FOSS.

-- 
Sandip(sandip@deeproot.co.in)

?. ???? ??????? wrote:

> I hope its possible to connect a laptop to a desktop for simply file
> sharing purposes without any switch in between.
> 
> now this is the scenario.. very simple i believe.. but missing out some
> where..
> 
> i have a laptop with kubuntu edgy
> i have a desktop with edubuntu feisty
> i have a rj-45 cable...

You should be using a cross-over cable to connect a laptop directly to a
desktop without a switch.

> NFS installed in both the machines...
> 
> do i need to do something in /etc/network/interfaces ? or change/ add/
> edit hosts ?
> 
> what else need to be done to make my pc talk to my laptop for file
> sharing purpose..

Once you connect using a cross over cable, assign IP addresses in the
same network for them and you can access one from the other. You said
that you have setup NFS already and that should help in sharing files.
But I would prefer running ssh and do scp/sshfs when needed.

Praveen.

For your case ofcourse its rj-45 , since your card accepts only that.

DA = 6% of Basic Pay
Vehicle Allowances (VA) = 2.4% of Basic Pay
Professional Tax(PT) = 1% of Basic Pay
PF = 12 % of Basic Pay
Net_pay = Basic+pay + HRA + DA + VA - PF - PT

I am sorry if this is not the correct place to ask this query.

indu veni wrote:
> Hi,
>
>  I dont know anything in perl. But I want answer to the following
question. Can some one please send me the code fo the following.
>
> 1) A perl program that records a file with the 4 fields from the
database. The fields are Emp_code, Emp_name, Basic_pay
> Also program to find the following:
>
> HRA = 12% of Basic Pay
> DA = 6% of Basic Pay
> Vehicle Allowances (VA) = 2.4% of Basic Pay
> Professional Tax(PT) = 1% of Basic Pay
> PF = 12 % of Basic Pay
> Net_pay = Basic+pay + HRA + DA + VA - PF - PT
>
> I am sorry if this is not the correct place to ask this query.
>
Lemme try to put it in an alternate way - You have a database with the
following fields - Emp_code, Emp_name, Basic_pay. And using the
database you want to calculate the above listed values which are based
on the Basic_pay or values calculated out of it for every employee
(and do you want the found values to be added to the database, i.e.
the record for the corresponding employee?)

Check this tutorial -
http://perl.about.com/od/perltutorials/a/perlmysql_3.htm

If you are looking for a flat file database (i.e. the fields are
stored in a file rather than a database) please check this link -
http://www.thescripts.com/serversidescripting/perl/tutorials/asimpledatabaseprogram/index.html

Seeing your question, this either seems to be some kind of assignment
or a question in an interview. So, IMHO it is better you learn how to
write the code than some one giving you the code and you just mugging
it up and presenting it. This is important because if they ask you to
do some modifications and run the code, if you do not know how to
write the code you will stumble badly.

From rajagopal.n at gmail.com  Mon May 14 19:34:21 2007
From: rajagopal.n at gmail.com (Rajagopal Natarajan)
Date: Mon May 14 19:34:34 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] imagecreate() problem..!
In-Reply-To: <6ef305610705132301s32595668h57eaa466960eb931@mail.gmail.com>
References: <6ef305610705132301s32595668h57eaa466960eb931@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <e0900f3e0705140704w6608a1c8mdd8dfc742ba57bcf@mail.gmail.com>

On 5/14/07, Suresh Kumar <suresh1876@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> hi
> i am facing some problem while creating JPEG image
>
> the error i get is
>
> Warning: imagecreatefromjpeg() [function.imagecreatefromjpeg]: gd-jpeg:
> JPEG
> library reports unrecoverable error:


Imagecreatefromjpeg() doesn't support CMYK JPEGs.

http://in.php.net/manual/en/function.imagecreatefromjpeg.php#55402

If you get this error: "Warning: imagecreatefromjpeg(): gd-jpeg: JPEG
> library reports unrecoverable error" then check the JPEG files. If they are
> saved in CMYK format (instead of RGB) then GD will fail to load them (tested
> with GD 2.0.12)



-- 
N. Rajagopal,
Visit me at http://users.kaski-net.net/~raj/

From kode at returnable.org  Thu May 17 10:03:33 2007
From: kode at returnable.org (Bhasker Kode)
Date: Thu May 17 10:03:44 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Returnable - Spawning javascript code with just a simple
	html API
Message-ID: <3935b63b0705162133s6bf89a58oc510bbb5911da7b2@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

I just wanted to share with everyone a new project that i'm launching today
called the Returnable Project ( http://returnable.org )

Returnable serves as a open-platform architectural guide to advance the use
of the URL as a DSL for specifying 3 traits : content,its delivery ,and its
behaviour on the web through the use of Returnable elements embedded within
web pages .

It's a personal project but quite a bit of javascript ,php ,url rewrite
,regex and css hacking spread over a few months of research and prototypes .

You could call it a way to create events using html as the API,if you have
the initial script added to the DOM.here is a simple example .

step1: add the script
<script type="text/javascript" src="http://returnable.org/returnable-core.js
"></script>

step2: add a returnable elements
<span><returnable href='
http://onhover.local.returnable.org/tooltip.text/this is somethin/'>Hover
over this for a cool tooltip</returnable></span>
<span><returnable href='
http://onclick.local.returnable.org/tooltip.text/this is somethin/'>Hover
over this for a cool tooltip</returnable></span>

=> thats it ! ... some of the afvantages are that u can have line breaks,
future version will also have html. With this architecture in place, the
simple text can be replaced with content from another source.

This is a proof of concept. It can be particularly used by bloggers who
need'nt code . just give the corresponing html . as of the launch today
,only tooltip return types exists. others to be added are - alerts ,
widgets,maps and so on.

For bloggers who are looking for an easy way to have tooltips (in javascript
enabled blogs) ,this could nbe a great utility. You can go through the site
to see demos on how to create intuitive tooltips (and more apps coming soon)
with just one line of code (apart from the script node to be added initially
)

I finally have the working prototypes ,and the project website website on
sourceforge,as well as the official website (returnable.org) running . I
plan to add support for oprea,(ie ,ff as of now ) , add mroe return types,
documentation ,etc .


----------------------------------------------------
Official website
http://returnble.org

My blog post announcement
http://bosky101.blogspot.com/2007/05/introducing-returnable-project.html

sourceforge project
http://sourceforge.net/projects/returnable/ .
----------------------------------------------------

Keep Clicking,

Bhasker V Kode
Lead Architect, The Returnable Project
kode at returnable.org

On 5/19/07, Ashok Kumar <ashok.grpmail@gmail.com> wrote:

> your suggestion?

Look at networking projects that require help:

http://sf.net
http://freshmeat.net
http://savannah.gnu.org

> which s/w will be the best one(in terms of small code size,

Start of by looking at bug reports. Try to solve the bugs. Submit
patches. This will give you a feel of the code. You can then look at
development.

> mostly and widely
> used s/w) which i can contribute easily.

It depends on which language/platform the project is implemented in,
and what you are comfortable with. So, just check out the network
monitoring projects in the sites mentioned above and pick one.

Have fun,

Subject: [Ilugc] protocol stack development
In-Reply-To: <d489eaf10705190452x449ce77fk7bf9d6ea90a4f250@mail.gmail.com>
References: <d489eaf10705190452x449ce77fk7bf9d6ea90a4f250@mail.gmail.com>

On 5/19/07, Ashok Kumar <ashok.grpmail@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> hi
> what is done under the name of protocol stack development in the industry?
> is it limited to the top three layers of the OSI model?


AFAIK implementation-wise, ppl dont follow OSI stack. Its only for
theoretical purposes(correct me if i'm wrong) ie., Most real-world protocol
stacks dont differentiate between the application, presentation and session
layers. Mostly TCP/IP stack model is followed. ie., those layers are put
together as one.

http://lejos.sourceforge.net/tutorial/communication/protocolstack.html
http://bro-ids.org/wiki/index.php/BinPAC

From riyaz.list at gmail.com  Sun May 20 15:05:27 2007
From: riyaz.list at gmail.com (Mohammed Riyaz)
Date: Sun May 20 15:05:37 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: protocol stack development
Message-ID: <622912820705200235r740c8fefuf506aa1af81a3c54@mail.gmail.com>

Hi Ashok,

>what is done under the name of protocol stack development in the industry?
>is it limited to the top three layers of the OSI model?

No, the work is not restricted to the application layer. There is a
lot of work being done at layer2/3. Generally companies don't write
the whole stack because it involves a lot of work. Most of the
companies buy the protocol stacks from vendors and port it to their
platform.

As an example, here is a vendor who sells stacks:
http://www.futsoft.com/protocol_stacks.htm

So most of the work will involve porting and fixing bugs in the stack
or developing the stack if you work in a product based company.

Similarly there is a lot of stack work happening in the telecom
industry as well.

Regards,
Riyaz

On 5/20/07, Rajagopal Natarajan <rajagopal.n@gmail.com> wrote:
> There is work, but do ppl separate the work in layers 2 and 3 from the
> application layer?

Yes, very much. For ex. if you are working on a router or a switch
your work will mainly involve only L2/L3 work. You might be working on
routing/switching protocols and you will not be concerned about the
application payload at all.

On 5/21/07, Shrinivasan T <tshrinivasan@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> Friends.
>
> I have kubuntu feisty fawn.
> At booting up, It should show "Kubuntu" image and a progress bar.
>

> login
> kdm window.
>

>
> How to solve this problem?


 sudo dpkg-reconfigure usplash

Incase any splash package configuration problem, it may get rectified..

 Incase u have installed more than one usplash screen(may be from edubuntu
artwork, or ubuntu artwork), do the following before the above.
 sudo update-alternatives --config usplash-artwork.so

That is what the article says! You need to work to get it running on
Linux while the vendor works to get it running on Windows. And when I
pay anything more than Rs.500 for a piece of hardware and it does not
work, it pains. To be honest, I am still researching to get my onboard
nvidia card to work with direct rendering, which has cost me a couple
of reinstalls, kernel downgrades, internet time and what not!!! I bet
my dad would not spend a minute like that. And I picked that board
even before I heard of what Linux is!

And that is likely what will happen with most people who are trying to
switch OS, at least for the cost factor involved! Just my opinion.

On 5/20/07, Rajagopal Natarajan <rajagopal.n@gmail.com> wrote:

>
> There is work, but do ppl separate the work in layers 2 and 3 from the
> application layer? Does any real world implementation exist where
> application layer interacts with layer 2 and 3 that exist separately,
> instead of enclosing those layer's work in itself?
>
>
>
> --


what about when you manufacture a lan card.
MAC has a specific layer.
tcp/ip are maybe coupled though they are in different layers.
But still thats a separate layer.
if you are writing a web server  you will be using the tcp/ip
implementation(probably) but not recreating it.
Difference of layers do exist. But the study of layers itself is just
academical as you said.
The developers who work with a particular layer are not required to be
concerned about the position of this layer in the stack or what is
above or below it.
Thats exactly why it has been divided into layers :)

From linux at frodo.hserus.net  Wed May 23 13:01:32 2007
From: linux at frodo.hserus.net (Suresh Ramasubramanian)
Date: Wed May 23 13:01:15 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] domain migration how to ?
In-Reply-To: <902eb7080705222345q77ae4a4dve5cedc54c228d250@mail.gmail.com>
References: <902eb7080705222345q77ae4a4dve5cedc54c228d250@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <4653EDD4.2040706@frodo.hserus.net>

vasudevan rk wrote:
>      Can i get a idea about migrating a domain from one server to another
> without changing Domain Name and Name Servers(NS)(i,e. i've placed a domain
> in ONE server www.guitarvasu.info which has the name server entry as
> ns1.tsrinivasan.com&ns2.tsrinivasan.com. I've planned to move the domain
> guitarvasu.info to anotherserver )

1. Set a short ttl for the A and MX records for guitarvasu.com (10m)

2. Once the ttl takes effect (if the old TTL is 1 day then next day):
	a. Change MX record to point to the new mailserver host
	b. Change A record to point to the new IP
	c. Config the new box's mailserver to host mail for your domain

From prem at songbirdtech.com  Wed May 23 17:06:45 2007
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)
Date: Wed May 23 17:06:59 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Five crucial things the Linux community doesn't 
	understand about the average computer user
Message-ID: <55666.61.247.255.57.1179920205.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

I think one of the things that the linux community does not understand
about ordinary users is that:

1) Installing new hardware and setting it up is still a very geeky
activity on Linux. Regular users want to buy and use a new printer, web
cam, scanner, mouse, monitor, DSL connection etc without having to monkey
around with CUPS, monitor modprobing, kernel recompiling etc. Most users
are not even keen on reading the installation manuals that come with their
DSL connections. They want to pop in a CD and click on "setup" and be done
with  the installation of the software, drivers etc.

To ask them to go through some obscure site on the net and wade through
some discussion forums just to get their new monitor/printer/DSL modem/etc
recognized properly is asking for too much.

And even for those few users who actually bother to read installation
manuals that come with their hardware, the manuals are mostly targeted at
windows users.

2) For most people, OS is not a religion. Most users won't even know what
is an OS and neither do they care to know. They don't really care about
this so called FREE-as-in-FREEDOM OS if their printer is not ready to work
in 5 minutes after they have connected it to their computers.

3) You get very little support if you call up BSNL/Airtel etc and ask why
your DSL modem is not working with the Linux distro installed on your
machine.

4) Games. Need I say more. To say that OpenGL on Linux is any comparison
to DirectX is to be totally deluded. OpenGL covers a minute subset of the
functionality that is there in DirectX 9. And now DirectX 10 is out and
there is no comparison at all. For those who disagree, please consider
looking at the Crysis Engine 2 or any other upcoming DirectX 10 titles.

If someone wants Unix, but yet wants to run their usual desktop app, then
I would recommend Mac OSX and not Linux. If money is a problem, I would
ask them to compromise and go for Linux.

regards,
PK

From bhasker at unixindia.com  Thu May 24 00:03:32 2007
From: bhasker at unixindia.com (Bhasker C V)
Date: Thu May 24 00:03:40 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] grub not able to detect window XP!
In-Reply-To: <4653EF98.8040400@gmail.com>
References: <10172.122.169.158.181.1179047843.squirrel@mail.sqlstar.com>
	<b2600ec40705130952p42be52fcrdd5b528e0aa7a586@mail.gmail.com>
	<10247.122.169.155.235.1179159058.squirrel@mail.sqlstar.com>
	<4653EF98.8040400@gmail.com>
Message-ID: <1179945212.5409.5.camel@h1.unixindia.com>

If you have data in the machine you must be careful.
But I usually use this step to recover

1. Use the windows boot disk and boot from CD
2. somewhere during the start of installation it will ask for selecte
Reparir
3. You select going to the microsoft repair console. 
4. You will get a command prompt. 
5. There is a command  "fixboot". This will fix your boot record.

Go to linux and then type

rootnoverify /dev/sda1
chainloader +1

and boot into windows.


Now, for the NTFS partition error,

1. In the same microsoft repair console DOS prompt, type chkdsk 
   chkdsk can fix most of the problems but sometimes you may lose
   data too.


Be doubly careful before doing any changes to the disk if you have a lot
of data in the disk. Try read-only mount of the ntfs partition on linux
and also try some ntfs recoery tools if you can grab hold of one.
Most of the times, the problem will get solved with chkdsk + fixboot. 
All the best !

From m.sujith at gmail.com  Thu May 24 10:53:00 2007
From: m.sujith at gmail.com (Sujith Manoharan)
Date: Thu May 24 10:53:15 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Structure copy behaviour
Message-ID: <1179984180.8607.24.camel@sujith-lnx>

Hi,

Say I have a structure :

typedef struct {
	...
	...
	...
} tmp;

And I do this :

tmp a[256];
tmp t;

a[0] = t;

Now, for this structure copy how does gcc decide that :

1) It should generate a call to memcpy
2) Generate instructions to manually do the copy.

What is the threshold for the structure's size that changes gcc's
behaviour ?
And is there any gcc parameter to change this threshold value ?

regards,
Sujith.

From vaidhy at loonys.net  Thu May 24 12:22:11 2007
From: vaidhy at loonys.net (Vaidhy)
Date: Thu May 24 12:22:26 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Structure copy behaviour
In-Reply-To: <1179984180.8607.24.camel@sujith-lnx>
References: <1179984180.8607.24.camel@sujith-lnx>
Message-ID: <e001dc80705232352u21f8fd63ydd548296fee81c51@mail.gmail.com>

>From what I remember, gcc always does a shallow copy (case 1) and as an
optimization, it implements copy-on-write.

Basically, assigning a[0] = t will have t and a[0] pointed to the same
location till you change either t or a[0]. At that point, there will be a
memcpy for sizeof(tmp) from &t to &a[0] and then the write will happen.

If you want to have a deep copy, only option I can think of right now is to
do it in C++ and implement the copy constructor and also overload the
assignment operator. (this is your case 2).

Regards,
Vaidhy

PS: My C and C++ are kind of rusty since I have not coded in them for the
last 4+ years. If things have changed since then, someone will be able to
correct it :)

> 
> If you want to have a deep copy, only option I can think of right now is to
> do it in C++ and implement the copy constructor and also overload the
> assignment operator. (this is your case 2).

Hmm.

Can you compile this program using the following command and take a look
at test.s ?

gcc -save-temps test.c [ without any optimization flags ]

#include <stdio.h>

typedef struct {
	char val[64];
} tmp;

int main()
{
	tmp a[256];
	tmp i;
	a[0]=i;
	return 0;
}

Now change val[64] to anything higher, say val[68] and look at test.s
now. All the movl instructions have been replaced by a single call to
memcpy.

Is there a way to change this behaviour ?

regards,
Sujith.

From vaidhy at loonys.net  Thu May 24 20:21:26 2007
From: vaidhy at loonys.net (Vaidhy)
Date: Thu May 24 20:21:35 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Structure copy behaviour
In-Reply-To: <1179991681.8607.35.camel@sujith-lnx>
References: <1179984180.8607.24.camel@sujith-lnx>
	<e001dc80705232352u21f8fd63ydd548296fee81c51@mail.gmail.com>
	<1179991681.8607.35.camel@sujith-lnx>
Message-ID: <e001dc80705240751m4ef21295h7ebe4dc2d426f75b@mail.gmail.com>

Took me a bit to find out.. but here is the reason:

gcc replaces calls to structure copy and pass by value copies with a call to
a library call (memset and memcpy). That is the reason for you getting
different assembly code for char[64] and char[68]. It is not a compile time
option you can change. However, according to what I read, the code is in
asm-i386.h in function struct_cpy. The following post might help you better
:)

http://groups.google.co.in/group/fa.linux.kernel/browse_thread/thread/78b3bcaa2ba884f0/f08a4653d7eb5908?lnk=st&q=gcc+memcpy+64+bytes&rnum=5&hl=en#

Cheers,
Vaidhy

On 5/24/07, Sujith Manoharan <m.sujith@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> On Thu, 2007-05-24 at 12:22 +0530, Vaidhy wrote:
> > From what I remember, gcc always does a shallow copy (case 1) and as an
> > optimization, it implements copy-on-write.
> >
> > Basically, assigning a[0] = t will have t and a[0] pointed to the same
> > location till you change either t or a[0]. At that point, there will be
> a
> > memcpy for sizeof(tmp) from &t to &a[0] and then the write will happen.
> >
> > If you want to have a deep copy, only option I can think of right now is
> to
> > do it in C++ and implement the copy constructor and also overload the
> > assignment operator. (this is your case 2).
>
> Hmm.
>
> Can you compile this program using the following command and take a look
> at test.s ?
>
> gcc -save-temps test.c [ without any optimization flags ]
>
> #include <stdio.h>
>
> typedef struct {
>         char val[64];
> } tmp;
>
> int main()
> {
>         tmp a[256];
>         tmp i;
>         a[0]=i;
>         return 0;
> }
>
> Now change val[64] to anything higher, say val[68] and look at test.s
> now. All the movl instructions have been replaced by a single call to
> memcpy.
>
> Is there a way to change this behaviour ?
>
> regards,
> Sujith.
>
>
> _______________________________________________
> To unsubscribe, email ilugc-request@ae.iitm.ac.in with
> "unsubscribe <password> <address>"
> in the subject or body of the message.
> http://www.ae.iitm.ac.in/mailman/listinfo/ilugc
>
From srivasta at debian.org  Thu May 24 20:22:58 2007
From: srivasta at debian.org (Manoj Srivastava)
Date: Thu May 24 20:30:27 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Five crucial things outsiders do not understand about the
	Linux community
References: <55666.61.247.255.57.1179920205.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>
Message-ID: <87ps4qtgs5.fsf@glaurung.internal.golden-gryphon.com>

On Wed, 23 May 2007 17:06:45 +0530 (IST), Prem Kurian Philip <prem@songbirdtech.com> said: 

> I think one of the things that the linux community does not understand
> about ordinary users is that:

        I think that people who write things like this have no clue
 about what drives the Linux community.  The lack of understanding of
 what drives free software developers 

> 1) Installing new hardware and setting it up is still a very geeky
>    activity on Linux.

  1) A computer is an expensive, useful, general purpose
     tool. Researching the purchase of the machine and peripherals for
     compatibility seems reasonable.  As long as it is possible to
     accomplish the task with some hardware, it does not matter that
     some hardware vendors make incompatible equipment.

        Actually, I think it is easier than getting  things not blessed
 by the Vendor to work on Vista.  And now that some hardware
 manufacturers are pre-installing Linux, it means that drivers are often
 available (Dell distributes their printer driver for my color laser as
 a GPL'd .deb).

        Frankly, I would not buy hardware before learning whether it
 supports Linux; and boycott the other hardware vendors.

> 2) For most people, OS is not a religion. Most users won't even know
>    what is an OS and neither do they care to know.
  2) Free software is about community; and people who care and
     participate, it is not a marketing machine; it is a group of people
     getting together to help each other achieve more from computers.

        These people are not part of the free software community, and I
 see no real reason to try to cater to them.  Free software is about
 community; is it surprising that no extraordinary effort is made to
 pander to those who are resistant to inclusion?

        Again, this is not about gaining market share.

> 3) You get very little support if you call up BSNL/Airtel etc and ask
>    why your DSL modem is not working with the Linux distro installed
>    on your  machine.
  3) The free software community helps each other; and the network has
     the results of people sharing how they made things work, and the
     pitfalls to avoid.

        ISP's, retail shop salespeople, hardware vendors might not be
 clued in to free software, which is only recently encroaching into the
 mainstream, but the community provides its own resources to each
 other. This is why this LUG is here, and why people participate.

> 4) Games. Need I say more. To say that OpenGL on Linux is any
>    comparison  to DirectX is to be totally deluded.
  4) Free software is not everything for all people.

        I've generally been very happy with nethack, angband, and tome,
 since I don't do twitch games, but I realize that this is not what
 people want. I've been OK with Worl of Warcraft using cedega and
 transgaming wine emulators.

   5) Free software is written by people who have an itch to scratch,
      and for like minded people. The basis is what I label as "The
      Dinid Philosophers Solution" -- it is written for other people who
      pick up the fork and help feed each other.


        Feeding hangers on who just want a free meal is not really a
 primary motivation.  Sure, having the meal in the open where anyone can
 pick up a fork lets new fork-weilders join in, but making extraordinary
 effort to feed the non-participating is not something very likely to
 happen on a broad scale.

        manoj
--

Main Entry: r??su?m?

* Manoj Srivastava <srivasta@debian.org> 2007-05-24
> On Wed, 23 May 2007 17:06:45 +0530 (IST), Prem Kurian Philip <prem@songbirdtech.com> said: 
> 
> > I think one of the things that the linux community does not understand
> > about ordinary users is that:
> 
>         I think that people who write things like this have no clue
>  about what drives the Linux community.  The lack of understanding of
>  what drives free software developers 

Some proverb (I don't remember which one, someone who knows let me know)
says that rain benefits everyone on earth, irrespective of who they are.
Similarly, we want free software to benefit everybody, without requiring
them to understand software and hardware. Examples: five-to-ten year-old
kids, sixty-years-and-older people. This requires some effort on our part,
and the benefits are worth it.

Also, computers are becoming ubiquitous
<http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ubiquitous_computing>, and we want those
computers to run free software. Otherwise, we will be forced to use
proprietary software. Replacing proprietary software is easier on desktop
computers, it is tougher on embedded systems.

-- 
Masatran, R. Deepak <http://research.iiit.ac.in/~masatran/>

On Thu, 2007-05-24 at 20:21 +0530, Vaidhy wrote:
> Took me a bit to find out.. but here is the reason:
> 
> gcc replaces calls to structure copy and pass by value copies with a call to
> a library call (memset and memcpy). That is the reason for you getting
> different assembly code for char[64] and char[68]. It is not a compile time
> option you can change. However, according to what I read, the code is in
> asm-i386.h in function struct_cpy. The following post might help you better
> :)
> 
> http://groups.google.co.in/group/fa.linux.kernel/browse_thread/thread/78b3bcaa2ba884f0/f08a4653d7eb5908?lnk=st&q=gcc+memcpy+64+bytes&rnum=5&hl=en#
>

On 5/24/07, Vaidhy <vaidhy@loonys.net> wrote:
> Took me a bit to find out.. but here is the reason:
>
> gcc replaces calls to structure copy and pass by value copies with a call to
> a library call (memset and memcpy). That is the reason for you getting
> different assembly code for char[64] and char[68]. It is not a compile time
> option you can change. However, according to what I read, the code is in
> asm-i386.h in function struct_cpy. The following post might help you better
> :)
>

I don't find asm-i386.h
I grepped for struct_cpy and found it in asm-i386/string-486.h

#define struct_cpy(x,y)                         \
({                                              \
        if (sizeof(*(x)) != sizeof(*(y)))       \
                __struct_cpy_bug;               \
        memcpy(x, y, sizeof(*(x)));             \
})

Is this the definition that you are talking about and will changing
this definition will it help ?

> http://groups.google.co.in/group/fa.linux.kernel/browse_thread/thread/78b3bcaa2ba884f0/f08a4653d7eb5908?lnk=st&q=gcc+memcpy+64+bytes&rnum=5&hl=en#
>
> Cheers,

> Cheers,
> Vaidhy
>
> On 5/24/07, Sujith Manoharan <m.sujith@gmail.com> wrote:
>>
>> On Thu, 2007-05-24 at 12:22 +0530, Vaidhy wrote:
>> > From what I remember, gcc always does a shallow copy (case 1) and as
>> an
>> > optimization, it implements copy-on-write.
>> >
>> > Basically, assigning a[0] = t will have t and a[0] pointed to the same
>> > location till you change either t or a[0]. At that point, there will
>> be
>> a
>> > memcpy for sizeof(tmp) from &t to &a[0] and then the write will
>> happen.
>> >
>> > If you want to have a deep copy, only option I can think of right now
>> is
>> to
>> > do it in C++ and implement the copy constructor and also overload the
>> > assignment operator. (this is your case 2).
>>
>> Hmm.
>>
>> Can you compile this program using the following command and take a look
>> at test.s ?
>>
>> gcc -save-temps test.c [ without any optimization flags ]
>>
>> #include <stdio.h>
>>
>> typedef struct {
>>         char val[64];
>> } tmp;
>>
>> int main()
>> {
>>         tmp a[256];
>>         tmp i;
>>         a[0]=i;
>>         return 0;
>> }
>>
>> Now change val[64] to anything higher, say val[68] and look at test.s
>> now. All the movl instructions have been replaced by a single call to
>> memcpy.
>>
>> Is there a way to change this behaviour ?
>>
>> regards,
>> Sujith.

>> about ordinary users is that:
>
>         I think that people who write things like this have no clue
>  about what drives the Linux community.  The lack of understanding of
>  what drives free software developers
>
>> 1) Installing new hardware and setting it up is still a very geeky
>>    activity on Linux.
>
>   1) A computer is an expensive, useful, general purpose
>      tool. Researching the purchase of the machine and peripherals for
>      compatibility seems reasonable.  As long as it is possible to
>      accomplish the task with some hardware, it does not matter that
>      some hardware vendors make incompatible equipment.
>
>         Actually, I think it is easier than getting  things not blessed
>  by the Vendor to work on Vista.  And now that some hardware
>  manufacturers are pre-installing Linux, it means that drivers are often
>  available (Dell distributes their printer driver for my color laser as
>  a GPL'd .deb).
>
>         Frankly, I would not buy hardware before learning whether it
>  supports Linux; and boycott the other hardware vendors.
>
>> 2) For most people, OS is not a religion. Most users won't even know
>>    what is an OS and neither do they care to know.
>   2) Free software is about community; and people who care and
>      participate, it is not a marketing machine; it is a group of people
>      getting together to help each other achieve more from computers.
>
>         These people are not part of the free software community, and I
>  see no real reason to try to cater to them.  Free software is about
>  community; is it surprising that no extraordinary effort is made to
>  pander to those who are resistant to inclusion?
>
>         Again, this is not about gaining market share.
>
>> 3) You get very little support if you call up BSNL/Airtel etc and ask
>>    why your DSL modem is not working with the Linux distro installed
>>    on your  machine.
>   3) The free software community helps each other; and the network has
>      the results of people sharing how they made things work, and the
>      pitfalls to avoid.
>
>         ISP's, retail shop salespeople, hardware vendors might not be
>  clued in to free software, which is only recently encroaching into the
>  mainstream, but the community provides its own resources to each
>  other. This is why this LUG is here, and why people participate.
>
>> 4) Games. Need I say more. To say that OpenGL on Linux is any
>>    comparison  to DirectX is to be totally deluded.
>   4) Free software is not everything for all people.
>
>         I've generally been very happy with nethack, angband, and tome,
>  since I don't do twitch games, but I realize that this is not what
>  people want. I've been OK with Worl of Warcraft using cedega and
>  transgaming wine emulators.
>
>    5) Free software is written by people who have an itch to scratch,
>       and for like minded people. The basis is what I label as "The
>       Dinid Philosophers Solution" -- it is written for other people who
>       pick up the fork and help feed each other.
>
>
>         Feeding hangers on who just want a free meal is not really a
>  primary motivation.  Sure, having the meal in the open where anyone can
>  pick up a fork lets new fork-weilders join in, but making extraordinary
>  effort to feed the non-participating is not something very likely to
>  happen on a broad scale.

2007/5/25, Masatran, R. Deepak <masatran@research.iiit.ac.in>:
> Replacing proprietary software is easier on desktop
> computers, it is tougher on embedded systems.
>

We are already seeing more and more embedded systems coming with Free
Software and it will be 100% real soon (Eben Moglen predicts it is
within 5 years and I agree with him).

"Now we have forty percent of the server market. We're going to have a
hundred percent of the appliance market within five years. That's a
trivial economic deduction from the following simple fact: when you
sell a four-hundred dollar palm top, you can afford to pay a license
fee for its operating system, of $24.95, or $49.95, or incur expensive
in-house development activity and make a Palm OS. When the box costs
fifty bucks, there's no room left for paying $12.95 to Mister Gates:
we win. We win."

Eben Moglen http://emoglen.law.columbia.edu/publications/maine-speech.html

Cheers
Praveen

graphics card and I didn't even notice I was missing something
(obviously I was not playing any games that require 3D support - I

and not even release the specs. Now we recommend everyone to use Intel
graphics cards, which has Free drivers for 3D support. When people
chose not to buy NVIDIA and ATI and go for Intel they will realise.

pre-installed and thye will go with only those hardware which work. So
this isn't much of an issue once more people start pre-installing
GNU/Linux like Dell.

You don't have to give substandard thing for your dad, but a system
with Intel motherboard and Intel graphics card with 3D support.

From arvindvanam at gmail.com  Fri May 25 13:25:47 2007
From: arvindvanam at gmail.com (arvind vanam)
Date: Fri May 25 13:25:57 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] bsnl dataone connection in SuSE
Message-ID: <a3bcf7260705250055r5d7d1260g697fdbf890933fdc@mail.gmail.com>

the procedure was quite simple for establishing BSNL DATAONE connection on
SuSE.

1)go to YaST
2)select network devices
3)click on DSL to create a broadband connection
4)add a dsl connection
5) in PPP mode select PPP over Ethernet
6)configure your ethernet card
             i)select the appropriate one
             ii)set the gateway as 192.168.1.1
             iii)you can set your own ip address or let DHCP provide you a
dynamic ip address .say set  it to 192.168.1.30.
            iv) you can set dns server ip by yourself if you want .the BSNL
service provide give you these details.or else the pppd will automatically
search for DNS and set
7)you can activate connection at boot time or you can do it manually.
8)now proceed to next step by providing name of the service
provider.setdataone(your choice)
9)set the user name and password for your connection
10)now select the checkbox for "automatically retrieve DNS" and "set DNS
automatically" if you havent set the DNS yourself.
11)proceed further and your dsl connection has been set.

a confirmation of this setup is that you get an icon on bottom panel
resempling a white coloured plug left-click on it to dial in and right click
to disconnect.

you can also set the DNS manually by editing /etc/resolv.conf and adding
lines as "nameserver xxx.yyy.zzz.www"

you can also manually start the connection by typing" ifup dsl0" at the
prompt in  terminal



i hope this helps those who are unable to connect to BSNL dataone in SuSE


Arvind Vanam

On 5/25/07, Sujith Manoharan <m.sujith@gmail.com> wrote:
> On Thu, 2007-05-24 at 20:21 +0530, Vaidhy wrote:
> > Took me a bit to find out.. but here is the reason:
> >
> > gcc replaces calls to structure copy and pass by value copies with a call to
> > a library call (memset and memcpy). That is the reason for you getting
> > different assembly code for char[64] and char[68]. It is not a compile time
> > option you can change. However, according to what I read, the code is in
> > asm-i386.h in function struct_cpy. The following post might help you better
> > :)
> >
> > http://groups.google.co.in/group/fa.linux.kernel/browse_thread/thread/78b3bcaa2ba884f0/f08a4653d7eb5908?lnk=st&q=gcc+memcpy+64+bytes&rnum=5&hl=en#
> >
>
>
> Thanks a lot for that link.
> And my problem is fixed now :)
>

Out of curiosity, was it your intention to change gcc's behaviour in
the struct copy case
If so what files did you change and did it involve recompiling gcc ?
